## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators and forced/damped vibration)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of time t and velocity v, which matches reduced forms of oscillator equations where the restoring-force/position is unobserved or absorbed into effective time-dependent forcing, and where dissipation/drive is modeled directly via velocity-dependent terms. Common structures include linear/nonlinear damping, dry friction, self-excitation (Rayleigh/van der Pol–type in v), and periodic/parametric forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear viscous damping (velocity relaxation): dv_dt = -c0 * v (small-amplitude linear drag or damping-dominated regime)
- Constant (bias) acceleration: dv_dt = c0 (constant external acceleration over the observation window)
- Dry/Coulomb friction (idealized): dv_dt = -c0 * sign(v) (velocity-independent friction opposing motion)
- Quadratic/turbulent drag: dv_dt = -c0 * v * Abs(v) (high-Reynolds-number drag-like dissipation)
- Nonlinear (cubic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v**3 (strong amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Rayleigh self-excited damping: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v (negative damping at small |v|, positive at large |v|)
- Smooth Coulomb friction (regularized): dv_dt = -c0 * tanh(c1 * v) (numerically stable approximation to sign(v))
- Linear damping + constant drive: dv_dt = -c0 * v + c1 (driven relaxation to a nonzero steady velocity)
- Periodic forcing only: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (external harmonic drive mapped into acceleration)
- Linear damping + harmonic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3) (damped, driven velocity dynamics)
- Multi-harmonic forcing (Fourier drive): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * cos(c1 * t) (generic periodic drive basis)
- Parametric (time-modulated) damping: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * v (damping coefficient varying periodically in time)
- Time-decaying drive (ring-down of forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * v + c1 * exp(-c2 * t) * sin(c3 * t + c4) (transient drive plus dissipation)
- Mixed nonlinear dissipation + forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * v * Abs(v) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (combined laminar+turbulent losses with periodic input)
- Liénard-in-v polynomial drift: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v**5 + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (generic normal-form style velocity dynamics with forcing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure dissipation with no drive typically yields dv_dt anti-aligned with v (negative drift), e.g., terms like -c*v, -c*v*Abs(v), -c*v**3.
- Dry friction shows near-constant-magnitude deceleration that flips sign at v=0; smooth proxies like tanh(c*v) reproduce the sharp transition without discontinuity.
- Quadratic drag is identified by odd symmetry and magnitude growing ~v^2 (dv_dt proportional to v*Abs(v)), producing faster decay at high speeds than linear damping.
- Self-excited oscillators often exhibit negative damping at small |v| but positive damping at large |v|, captured structurally by (c0 - v**2)*v (or higher odd polynomials).
- External periodic excitation appears as sin(c*t+c0)/cos(c*t+c0) additive terms; if dv_dt contains strong periodic components even when v≈0, forcing terms are likely.
- Parametric excitation/modulation is suggested when the coefficient multiplying v varies periodically in t, i.e., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*v, leading to time-varying decay rates.
- If trajectories show approach to a nonzero mean velocity, include an additive bias c0 or an affine drift -c1*v + c0 (relaxation to v* = c0/c1).
- Strong asymmetry between positive and negative velocities may require odd+even mixtures such as v*Abs(v) or tanh(c*v), rather than pure odd polynomials.
- When dv_dt exhibits transient oscillations whose amplitude decays over time, multiply harmonic forcing by exp(-c*t) (a decaying drive/forcing envelope rather than damping-only).

So any matching candidate must (i) have a pure \(\sin(t)\) term with constant amplitude, (ii) have a \(-\text{const}\cdot v^3\) term, and crucially (iii) have a \(\log(|v|+1)\) term (log of an affine function of \(|v|\), not \(\log(1+kv^2)\), not \(\log(1+\exp(\cdot))\), not multiplied by \(v\), etc.). Also no extra \(v\), \(v^2\), \(|v|\), piecewise Max terms, exponentials, etc., unless their coefficients can be set to 0.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO24)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*log(Abs(v) + c1)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.0834*v³ - 0.9954*log(|v| + 1) + 0.7824*sin(t)**

The key components are:
1. A **v³** term
2. A **log(|v| + 1)** term
3. A **sin(t)** term

Let me analyze the log(|v| + 1) term carefully. Note that:
- log(|v| + 1) is an even-like function but NOT exactly even (it's even in v)
- It cannot be represented by polynomials, v*|v|, |v|, Max(0,v), Max(0,-v), exp(v), etc.

Let me check which candidates have the right basis functions.

**Key question:** Can log(|v| + 1) be represented by combinations of other functions?

Note: log(|v| + 1) is symmetric in v (even function), smooth, and logarithmic. It cannot be exactly represented by:
- Polynomials (v², v⁴, etc.) - these grow polynomially
- v*|v| (odd function)
- Max(0,v) + Max(0,-v) = |v| (linear growth, not logarithmic)
- exp(v) terms
- v/sqrt(c + v²) (bounded, not logarithmic growth)

Let me check candidates with log terms:

**Candidate 12:** c0 + c1*exp(c2*v)*sin(c3+c4*t) + c5*v + c6*v³ + c7*log(c8*v²+1) + c9*v*|v|
- Set c1=0 (kill exp*sin), c5=0, c9=0. Get: c0 + c6*v³ + c7*log(c8*v²+1)
- Need log(c8*v²+1) ≡ log(|v|+1). But log(c8*v²+1) ≠ log(|v|+1) for any c8. These are fundamentally different functions.

**Candidate 13:** Similar with log(c8*v²+1) - same issue.

**Candidate 14, 15:** Same log(c*v²+1) issue.

**Candidate 22:** c7*log(c8*exp(c9*v)+1) - this is a softplus-like function, asymmetric in v. Cannot match log(|v|+1).

**Candidate 24:** c7*v*log(c8*|v|+1) - this is odd in v, while log(|v|+1) is even. Cannot match.

**Candidate 30:** c7*log(c8*exp(c9*v)+1) - softplus, same issue as 22.

**Candidate 50:** c0*v/(c1+v) + c2*log(c3*exp(c4*v+c5*sin(c6*t+c7))+1) + c8
- The log term mixes v and t through exp. Setting c5=0: c2*log(c3*exp(c4*v)+1). This is a softplus, not log(|v|+1).

For all candidates with Max(0,v), Max(0,-v), v*|v|, polynomials, exp terms - none can produce the logarithmic growth of log(|v|+1).

For candidates with only polynomial/piecewise-linear/exponential basis functions (Candidates 1-11, 16-21, 23, 25-29, 31-49): None have a log(|v|+1) term or anything equivalent.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates contain the basis function log(|v|+1) or anything that can be algebraically transformed to match it exactly.
